< user_name>
Garry Corret< /user_name>
<date>1569514397050</date><Rating>5<//Rating>< text>
If you've read or seen the film 'The Prestige', you'll be a fan of this slightly hidden from sight cocktail bar located in the newly renovated Robertson Plaza.

The cocktail menu is separated into the three parts of a magic trick - The Pledge, The Turn, and The Prestige. The Pledge focuses on the seemingly normal with slight variation made to the classics. The Turn transforms the seemingly normal to the extraordinary by turning the twist up a notch. The Prestige is the culminating final act that combines the lessons of the first two acts and spins up something even more grandeur; cocktails on this page focus on layering unique ingredients together to create a complex palette.

Behind the scenes, all the best practices of composing a standard craft cocktail follow. This includes the chilled glassware, the chipping away of large chunks of clear ice, and the right aromatic toppings.

The interior is beautifully decorated and follows an art deco look. Beautiful lighting decorate the cabinet fixtures and ceiling.

I had the Sing Sing from the Prestige page, which based on the name & ingredients seemed to be an evolution of the Singapore Sling. Unlike the usual sweetness of the Sling, the Sing balanced the taste and packed quite a punch. It was a refreshing kick to start the evening.</text>

<Pics>None< /Pics><Review>Bibo is hands down my favorite cocktail bar in this part of town! Yes, beauty is in the eye of the beholder, but I really dig the ambiance and the art deco decor. The entrance is semi-hidden, tucked away in the corner of a plaza. Can't speak too much about the food, but I would recommend nearly every drink I've had here. The drink menu is really quite creative the way the drinks are organized. Staff is knowledgable as well and can give great recommendations if you're unsure of what to order.

Note that they also have a stellar happy hour weekdays from 5-7pm with $6 martinis and $8 wines. When they first opened a bit over a year ago it was never too crowded, but it seems like more and more people have been stopping by as of late. I guess the secret is out!< /Review><Name>Hettie Mcneely</Name>< Time>

We're on our way from LA to Canada, and wanted something tasty and healthy after fast-food road junk had us all feeling icky. My wife found this place on Yelp, and it was near our hotel, so we gave it a go to take back to our hotel. It was VERY good. We're used to Baghdadi Mediterranean cuisine, and though this was different (Cypriot?), it was wonderful. The falafel sandwich was brilliant, and had a surprisingly little spicy kick to it. Very, very tasty. The hummus was ok, not great, not bad, but tasty enough. The prices were also just a tad, tad bit higher than we expected, but again, we really enjoyed the meal.< /Text>

< review>
After years of driving past I finally tried this place. It is prominently located on the end of a strip mall and see it every time I drive by.

So we go in and it is very spacious and well lit, there are no customers to be found. One lady, possibly the owner behind the counter. Selections were limited very basic Chinese food and didn't look the freshest. But I was in the mood for some Chinese so we tried it anyway.

The food was acceptable at best. We have been to other HKE locations and the food was much worse quality and quantity than the others.

I normally would give it a 3 star rating, but about 2 weeks after this visit I wanted Chinese again, and rather than driving to Cypress for our favourite HKE experience at 8:30 in the evening we just went up the street to the local La Mirada HKE. When we got there we were shocked, they were closed, the hours sign on the door said they should be open til 9, but the were closed... not just closed, but gone closed, everything cleaned up, lights off, doors locked, nobody home closed. Closed and gone at 8:35ish when they are supposed to be open til 9.

Sorry LM HKE... we will not be back. We drove to the Cypress HKE, got there a little after 9 and they were still open (also list 9 as closing time) selling off the remaining food. Which to me makes sense, why throw everything away when there are people who will buy it? Besides how hard it is to "stay open" while you are cleaning the kitchen and sell off the remaining food.< /review>
